<p><b>Amitabh Harivansh Rai Shrivastava Bachchan</b> (<small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA for Hindi and Urdu">[?m?'ta?b? 'b?t???n]</a></span>; born 11 October 1942) is an Indian film actor. He first gained popularity in the early 1970s for movies like <i><a href="/wiki/Zanjeer_(1973_film)" title="Zanjeer (1973 film)">Zanjeer</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Deewaar_(1975_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Deewaar (1975 film)">Deewaar</a></i>, and was dubbed India's first "angry young man" for his on-screen roles in <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>. Referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Shahanshah_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Shahanshah (disambiguation)">Shahenshah</a> of Bollywood", "Star of the Millennium" or "Big B",<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> he has since appeared in over 190 Indian films in a career spanning almost five decades.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-angryyoungman_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angryyoungman-8">[8]</a></sup> Bachchan is widely regarded as one of the greatest and most influential actors in the history of <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_India" title="Cinema of India">Indian cinema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> So total was his dominance on the movie scene in the 1970s and 1980s that the French director <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Truffaut" title="François Truffaut">François Truffaut</a> called him a "one-man industry."<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan has won <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Amitabh_Bachchan" title="List of awards and nominations received by Amitabh Bachchan">numerous accolades</a> in his career, including four <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards" title="National Film Awards">National Film Awards</a> as <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="National Film Award for Best Actor">Best Actor</a> and many awards at international film festivals and award ceremonies. He has won fifteen <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> and is the most-nominated performer in any major acting category at Filmfare, with 41 nominations overall. In addition to acting, Bachchan has worked as a <a href="/wiki/Playback_singer" title="Playback singer">playback singer</a>, film producer and television presenter. He has hosted several seasons of the game show, <a href="/wiki/Kaun_Banega_Crorepati" title="Kaun Banega Crorepati">Kaun Banega Crorepati</a>, India's version of the game show franchise, <a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Be_a_Millionaire%3F" title="Who Wants to Be a Millionaire?">Who Wants to Be a Millionaire?</a>. He also had a stint in politics in the 1980s.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> honoured him with the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Shri" title="Padma Shri">Padma Shri</a> in 1984, the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Bhushan" title="Padma Bhushan">Padma Bhushan</a> in 2001 and the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Vibhushan" title="Padma Vibhushan">Padma Vibhushan</a> in 2015 for his contributions to <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">the arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Padma_Awards_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Padma_Awards-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_France" title="Government of France">Government of France</a> honoured him with its highest civilian honour, Knight of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a>, in 2007 for his exceptional career in the world of cinema and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-Legion_of_Honour_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Legion_of_Honour-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan made his Hollywood debut in 2013 with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gatsby_(2013_film)" title="The Great Gatsby (2013 film)">The Great Gatsby</a></i>, in which he played a non-Indian Jewish character, Meyer Wolfsheim.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_and_personal_life">Early and personal life</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bachchan_family" title="Bachchan family">Bachchan family</a></div>
<p>Bachchan was born in <a href="/wiki/Allahabad" title="Allahabad">Allahabad</a>, Uttar Pradesh, in north central India.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> His ancestors hailed from a village called <a href="/wiki/Babupatti" title="Babupatti">Babupatti</a> in the Raniganj taluka of <a href="/wiki/Pratapgarh_district,_Uttar_Pradesh" title="Pratapgarh district, Uttar Pradesh">Pratapgarh district</a> in Uttar Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> His father <a href="/wiki/Harivansh_Rai_Bachchan" title="Harivansh Rai Bachchan">Harivansh Rai Srivastava (Bachchan)</a> was a well-known <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> poet and his mother <a href="/wiki/Teji_Bachchan" title="Teji Bachchan">Teji Bachchan</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Punjabis" title="Punjabis">Punjabi</a> <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a> from Lyallpur (now <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad" title="Faisalabad">Faisalabad</a>), <a href="/wiki/Punjab_Province_(British_India)" title="Punjab Province (British India)">Punjab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sikh_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sikh-21">[21]</a></sup> Bachchan was initially named <i>Inquilaab,</i> inspired by the phrase <i><a href="/wiki/Inquilab_Zindabad" title="Inquilab Zindabad">Inquilab Zindabad</a></i> popularly used during the Indian independence struggle. In English, <i>Inquilab Zindabad</i> means "Long live the revolution." However, at the suggestion of fellow poet <a href="/wiki/Sumitranandan_Pant" title="Sumitranandan Pant">Sumitranandan Pant</a>, Harivansh Rai changed the boy's name to Amitabh, which means "the light that will never die."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although his surname was <a href="/wiki/Srivastava" title="Srivastava">Shrivastava</a>, Amitabh's father had adopted the pen name Bachchan ("child-like" in colloquial Hindi), under which he published all of his works.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It is with this last name that Amitabh debuted in films and for all other practical purposes, Bachchan has become the surname for all of his immediate family.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Bachchan's father died in 2003, and his mother in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan is an alumnus of <a href="/wiki/Sherwood_College" title="Sherwood College">Sherwood College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nainital" title="Nainital">Nainital</a>. He later attended <a href="/wiki/Kirori_Mal_College" title="Kirori Mal College">Kirori Mal College</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Delhi" title="University of Delhi">University of Delhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> He has a younger brother, Ajitabh. His mother had a keen interest in theatre and was offered a feature film role, but she preferred her domestic duties. Teji had some influence in Amitabh Bachchan's choice of career because she always insisted that he should "take the centre stage."<sup id="cite_ref-AB_and_his_parents_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_and_his_parents-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan is married to actress <a href="/wiki/Jaya_Bachchan" title="Jaya Bachchan">Jaya Bhaduri</a>. The couple have two children, Shweta Nanda (wife of businessman <a href="/wiki/Nikhil_Nanda" title="Nikhil Nanda">Nikhil Nanda</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Abhishek_Bachchan" title="Abhishek Bachchan">Abhishek Bachchan</a> (actor and husband of actress <a href="/wiki/Aishwarya_Rai" title="Aishwarya Rai">Aishwarya Rai</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_work:_1969.E2.80.931972">Early work: 19691972</span></h3>
<p>Bachchan made his film debut in 1969 as a voice narrator in <a href="/wiki/Mrinal_Sen" title="Mrinal Sen">Mrinal Sen</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Feature_Film" title="National Film Award for Best Feature Film">National Award</a> winning film <i><a href="/wiki/Bhuvan_Shome" title="Bhuvan Shome">Bhuvan Shome</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> His first acting role was as one of the seven protagonists in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Saat_Hindustani" title="Saat Hindustani">Saat Hindustani</a></i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Khwaja_Ahmad_Abbas" title="Khwaja Ahmad Abbas">Khwaja Ahmad Abbas</a> and featuring <a href="/wiki/Utpal_Dutt" title="Utpal Dutt">Utpal Dutt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Ali_(actor)" title="Anwar Ali (actor)">Anwar Ali</a> (brother of comedian <a href="/wiki/Mehmood_(actor)" title="Mehmood (actor)">Mehmood</a>), <a href="/wiki/Madhu_(actor)" title="Madhu (actor)">Madhu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jalal_Agha" title="Jalal Agha">Jalal Agha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-First_national_award_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_national_award-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Anand_(1971_film)" title="Anand (1971 film)">Anand</a></i> (1971) followed, in which Bachchan starred alongside Rajesh Khanna. His role as a doctor with a cynical view of life garnered Bachchan his first Filmfare <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_for_supporting_actor" title="List of awards for supporting actor">Best Supporting Actor</a></i> award. He then played his first antagonist role as an infatuated lover-turned-murderer in <i><a href="/wiki/Parwana_(1971_film)" title="Parwana (1971 film)">Parwana</a></i> (1971). Following Parwaana were several films including <i><a href="/wiki/Reshma_Aur_Shera" title="Reshma Aur Shera">Reshma Aur Shera</a></i> (1971). During this time, he made a guest appearance in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Guddi_(1971_film)" title="Guddi (1971 film)">Guddi</a></i> which starred his future wife Jaya Bhaduri. He narrated part of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Bawarchi" title="Bawarchi">Bawarchi</a>.</i> In 1972 he made an appearance in the road action comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Bombay_to_Goa" title="Bombay to Goa">Bombay to Goa</a></i> directed by <a href="/wiki/S._Ramanathan" title="S. Ramanathan">S. Ramanathan</a>. Many of Bachchan's films during this early period did not do well, but that was about to change.<sup id="cite_ref-iconic1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iconic1-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_to_stardom:_1973.E2.80.931983">Rise to stardom: 19731983</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BigB_N_JayaB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BigB_N_JayaB.jpg/225px-BigB_N_JayaB.jpg" width="225" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BigB_N_JayaB.jpg/338px-BigB_N_JayaB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BigB_N_JayaB.jpg/450px-BigB_N_JayaB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="425" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BigB_N_JayaB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bachchan and wife <a href="/wiki/Jaya_Bhaduri" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaya Bhaduri">Jaya Bhaduri Bachchan</a> in 2013, the couple got married in 1973, after the release of <i>Zanjeer</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Director <a href="/wiki/Prakash_Mehra" title="Prakash Mehra">Prakash Mehra</a> cast him in the leading role for the film <i>Zanjeer</i> (1973) as Inspector Vijay Khanna. The film was a sharp contrast to the romantically themed films that had generally preceded it and established Amitabh in a new personathe "angry young man" of Bollywood cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-angryyoungman_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angryyoungman-8">[8]</a></sup> Filmfare considers this one of the most iconic performances of Bollywood history.<sup id="cite_ref-iconic1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iconic1-28">[28]</a></sup> The film was a huge success and one of the highest-grossing films of that year, breaking Bachchan's dry spell at the box office and making him a star.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> From then onwards, Bachchan became one of the most successful leading men of the film industry. He earned his first Filmfare nomination for Best Actor for <i>Zanjeer</i>. The year 1973 was also when he married Jaya, and around this time they appeared in several films together; not only in <i>Zanjeer</i> but in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Abhimaan_(1973_film)" title="Abhimaan (1973 film)">Abhimaan</a></i> which followed and was released only a month after their marriage and was also successful at the box office. Later, Bachchan played the role of Vikram, once again along with Rajesh Khanna, in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Namak_Haraam" title="Namak Haraam">Namak Haraam</a></i>, a social drama directed by <a href="/wiki/Hrishikesh_Mukherjee" title="Hrishikesh Mukherjee">Hrishikesh Mukherjee</a> and scripted by Biresh Chatterjee addressing themes of friendship. His supporting role won him his second Filmfare <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_for_supporting_actor" title="List of awards for supporting actor">Best Supporting Actor</a></i> award.</p>
<p>In 1974, Bachchan made several guest appearances in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kunwara_Baap_(1974_film)" title="Kunwara Baap (1974 film)">Kunwara Baap</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dost_(1974_film)" title="Dost (1974 film)">Dost</a></i>, before playing a supporting role in <i><a href="/wiki/Roti_Kapda_Aur_Makaan" title="Roti Kapda Aur Makaan">Roti Kapda Aur Makaan</a></i>. The film, directed and written by <a href="/wiki/Manoj_Kumar" title="Manoj Kumar">Manoj Kumar</a>, addressed themes of honesty in the face of oppression and financial and emotional hardship and was the top earning film of 1974. Bachchan then played the leading role in film <i><a href="/wiki/Majboor_(1974_film)" title="Majboor (1974 film)">Majboor</a></i>, released on 6 December 1974, which was a remake of the Hollywood film <i><a href="/wiki/Zig_Zag_(1970_film)" title="Zig Zag (1970 film)">Zig Zag</a></i>. The film was a success at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In 1975, he starred in a variety of film genres from the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Chupke_Chupke" title="Chupke Chupke">Chupke Chupke</a>,</i> the crime drama <i><a href="/wiki/Faraar" title="Faraar">Faraar</a></i> to the romantic drama <i><a href="/wiki/Mili_(1975_film)" title="Mili (1975 film)">Mili</a>.</i> 1975 was also the year when Bachchan appeared in two films regarded as important in Hindi cinema history. He starred in the <a href="/wiki/Yash_Chopra" title="Yash Chopra">Yash Chopra</a> directed film <i>Deewaar</i> along with <a href="/wiki/Shashi_Kapoor" title="Shashi Kapoor">Shashi Kapoor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nirupa_Roy" title="Nirupa Roy">Nirupa Roy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Neetu_Singh" title="Neetu Singh">Neetu Singh</a>, earning him a Filmfare nomination for Best Actor. The film became a major hit at the box office in 1975, ranking in at number 4.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <i>Indiatimes Movies</i> ranks <i>Deewaar</i> amongst the <i>Top 25 Must See Bollywood Films</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-mustsee_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mustsee-32">[32]</a></sup> Released on 15 August 1975 was <i><a href="/wiki/Sholay" title="Sholay">Sholay</a></i>, which became the highest-grossing film of 1975 and also of all time in India, earning <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">INR</a> 2,364,500,000 equivalent to US$60 million, after adjusting for inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-boxoffice_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice-33">[33]</a></sup> in which Bachchan played the role of Jaidev. In 1999, <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> India declared it the "Film of the Millennium" and like <i>Deewar</i>, has been cited by <i><a href="/wiki/Indiatimes" class="mw-redirect" title="Indiatimes">Indiatimes</a> movies</i> as amongst the <i>Top 25 Must See Bollywood Films</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-mustsee_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mustsee-32">[32]</a></sup> In that same year, the judges of the 50th annual Filmfare Awards awarded it with the special distinction award called Filmfare Best Film of 50 Years.</p>
<p>In 1976, he was cast by Yash Chopra in the romantic family drama <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhie_Kabhie_(1976_film)" title="Kabhie Kabhie (1976 film)">Kabhie Kabhie</a></i>. Bachchan starred as a young poet named Amit Malhotra who falls deeply in love with a beautiful young girl named Pooja (<a href="/wiki/Rakhee_Gulzar" title="Rakhee Gulzar">Rakhee Gulzar</a>) who ends up marrying someone else (<a href="/wiki/Shashi_Kapoor" title="Shashi Kapoor">Shashi Kapoor</a>). The film was notable for portraying Bachchan as a romantic hero, a far cry from his "angry young man" roles like <i>Zanjeer</i> and <i>Deewar</i>. The film evoked a favourable response from critics and audiences alike. Bachchan was again nominated for the Filmfare Best Actor Award for his role in the film. That same year he played a double role in <i><a href="/wiki/Adalat_(1976_film)" title="Adalat (1976 film)">Adalat</a></i> as father and son. In 1977, he won his first <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Filmfare Award for Best Actor">Filmfare Best Actor Award</a> for his performance in <i>Amar Akbar Anthony</i> where he played the third lead opposite <a href="/wiki/Vinod_Khanna" title="Vinod Khanna">Vinod Khanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rishi_Kapoor" title="Rishi Kapoor">Rishi Kapoor</a> as Anthony Gonsalves. The film was the highest-grossing film of that year. His other successes that year include <i><a href="/wiki/Parvarish_(1977_film)" title="Parvarish (1977 film)">Parvarish</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Khoon_Pasina" title="Khoon Pasina">Khoon Pasina</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> He once again resumed double roles in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kasme_Vaade" title="Kasme Vaade">Kasme Vaade</a></i> (1978) as Amit and Shankar and <i><a href="/wiki/Don_(1978_film)" title="Don (1978 film)">Don</a></i> (1978) playing the characters of Don, a leader of an underworld gang and his look alike Vijay. His performance won him his second Filmfare Best Actor Award. He also gave towering performances in Yash Chopra's <i><a href="/wiki/Trishul_(film)" title="Trishul (film)">Trishul</a></i> and Prakash Mehra's <i><a href="/wiki/Muqaddar_Ka_Sikandar" title="Muqaddar Ka Sikandar">Muqaddar Ka Sikandar</a></i> both of which earned him further Filmfare Best Actor nominations.</p>
<p>In 1979, Bachchan starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Suhaag_(1979_film)" title="Suhaag (1979 film)">Suhaag</a></i> which was the highest earning film of that year. In the same year he also enjoyed critical acclaim and commercial success with films like <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Natwarlal" title="Mr. Natwarlal">Mr. Natwarlal</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Kaala_Patthar" title="Kaala Patthar">Kaala Patthar</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gambler" title="The Great Gambler">The Great Gambler</a></i>. Amitabh was required to use his singing voice for the first time in a song from the film <i>Mr. Natwarlal</i> in which he starred with <a href="/wiki/Rekha" title="Rekha">Rekha</a>. Bachchan's performance in the film saw him nominated for both the Filmfare Best Actor Award and the <i><a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Male_Playback_Singer" title="Filmfare Award for Best Male Playback Singer">Filmfare Award for Best Male Playback Singer</a></i>. He also received Best Actor nomination for <i>Kaala Patthar</i> and then went on to be nominated again in 1980 for the <a href="/wiki/Raj_Khosla" title="Raj Khosla">Raj Khosla</a> directed film <i><a href="/wiki/Dostana_(1980_film)" title="Dostana (1980 film)">Dostana</a></i>, in which he starred opposite <a href="/wiki/Shatrughan_Sinha" title="Shatrughan Sinha">Shatrughan Sinha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zeenat_Aman" title="Zeenat Aman">Zeenat Aman</a>. <i>Dostana</i> proved to be the top-grossing film of 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In 1981, he starred in Yash Chopra's melodrama film <i><a href="/wiki/Silsila_(film)" title="Silsila (film)">Silsila</a></i>, where he starred alongside his wife Jaya and Rekha. Other films of this period like <i><a href="/wiki/Shaan_(film)" title="Shaan (film)">Shaan</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/Shakti_(1982_film)" title="Shakti (1982 film)">Shakti</a></i> (1982) which pitted him against the veteran actor <a href="/wiki/Dilip_Kumar" title="Dilip Kumar">Dilip Kumar</a> were not successful at the box office but <i><a href="/wiki/Ram_Balram" title="Ram Balram">Ram Balram</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/Naseeb_(1981_film)" title="Naseeb (1981 film)">Naseeb</a></i> (1981) and <i><a href="/wiki/Laawaris_(film)" title="Laawaris (film)">Lawaaris</a></i> (1981) were successful.<sup id="cite_ref-Box_office_success_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Box_office_success-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1982 he played double roles in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Satte_Pe_Satta" title="Satte Pe Satta">Satte Pe Satta</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Desh_Premee" title="Desh Premee">Desh Premee</a></i> which succeeded at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1983 he played a triple role in <i><a href="/wiki/Mahaan" title="Mahaan">Mahaan</a></i> and starred in the top-grossing film of that year <i><a href="/wiki/Coolie" title="Coolie">Coolie</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1982_injury_while_filming_Coolie">1982 injury while filming <i>Coolie</i></span></h3>
<p>On 26 July 1982, while filming <i><a href="/wiki/Coolie_(1983_Hindi_film)" title="Coolie (1983 Hindi film)">Coolie</a></i>,in the University Campus in Bangalore, Bachchan suffered a near fatal intestinal injury during the filming of a fight scene with co-actor <a href="/wiki/Puneet_Issar" title="Puneet Issar">Puneet Issar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Coolie_fight_scene_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coolie_fight_scene-39">[39]</a></sup> Bachchan was performing his own stunts in the film and one scene required him to fall onto a table and then on the ground. However, as he jumped towards the table, the corner of the table struck his abdomen, resulting in a <a href="/wiki/Splenic_injury" title="Splenic injury">splenic rupture</a> from which he lost a significant amount of blood. He required an emergency <a href="/wiki/Splenectomy" title="Splenectomy">splenectomy</a> and remained critically ill in hospital for many months, at times close to death. The public response included prayers in temples and offers to sacrifice limbs to save him, while later, there were long queues of well-wishing fans outside the hospital where he was recuperating.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nevertheless, he resumed filming later that year after a long period of recuperation. The film was released in 1983, and partly due to the huge publicity of Bachchan's accident, the film was a box office success and the top-grossing film that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Coolie_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coolie-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The director, <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Desai" title="Manmohan Desai">Manmohan Desai</a>, altered the ending of <i>Coolie</i> after Bachchan's accident. Bachchan's character was originally intended to have been killed off but after the change of script, the character lived in the end. It would have been inappropriate, said Desai, for the man who had just fended off death in real life to be killed on screen. Also, in the released film the footage of the fight scene is frozen at the critical moment, and a caption appears onscreen marking this as the instant of the actor's injury and the ensuing publicity of the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later, he was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Myasthenia_gravis" title="Myasthenia gravis">Myasthenia gravis</a>. His illness made him feel weak both mentally and physically and he decided to quit films and venture into politics. At this time he became pessimistic, expressing concern with how a new film would be received and stated before every release, "Yeh film to flop hogi!" ("This film will flop").<sup id="cite_ref-Myasthenia_Gravis_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Myasthenia_Gravis-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics:_1984.E2.80.9387">Politics: 198487</span></h3>
<p>In 1984, Bachchan took a break from acting and briefly entered politics in support of long-time family friend, <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi" title="Rajiv Gandhi">Rajiv Gandhi</a>. He contested Allahabad's seat of <a href="/wiki/8th_Lok_Sabha" title="8th Lok Sabha">8th Lok Sabha</a> against <a href="/wiki/Hemvati_Nandan_Bahuguna" title="Hemvati Nandan Bahuguna">H. N. Bahuguna</a>, former <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chief_Ministers_of_Uttar_Pradesh" title="List of Chief Ministers of Uttar Pradesh">Chief Minister of Uttar Pradesh</a> and won by one of the highest victory margins in <a href="/wiki/General_elections_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="General elections in India">general election history</a> (68.2% of the vote).<sup id="cite_ref-election_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-election-44">[44]</a></sup> His political career, however, was short-lived: he resigned after three years, calling politics a <a href="/wiki/Cesspit" title="Cesspit">cesspool</a>. The resignation followed the implication of Bachchan and his brother in the "<a href="/wiki/Bofors_scandal" title="Bofors scandal">Bofors scandal</a>" by a newspaper, which he vowed to take to court.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Bachchan was eventually found not guilty of involvement in the ordeal<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Your explanation here (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<p>His old friend, <a href="/wiki/Amar_Singh_(politician)" title="Amar Singh (politician)">Amar Singh</a>, helped him during the financial crisis caused by the failure of his company, <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan_Corporation" title="Amitabh Bachchan Corporation">ABCL</a>. Thereafter Bachchan started supporting the <a href="/wiki/Samajwadi_Party" title="Samajwadi Party">Samajwadi Party</a>, the political party to which Amar Singh belonged. Furthermore, Jaya Bachchan joined the Samajwadi party and represented the party as an MP in the <a href="/wiki/Rajya_Sabha" title="Rajya Sabha">Rajya Sabha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Bachchan has continued to do favours for the Samajwadi party, including appearing in advertisements and political campaigns. These activities have recently got him into trouble in the Indian courts for false claims after a previous incident of submission of legal papers by him, stating that he is a farmer.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 15-year press ban against Bachchan was imposed during his peak acting years by <i><a href="/wiki/Stardust_(magazine)" title="Stardust (magazine)">Stardust</a></i> and some of the other film magazines. In his defence, Bachchan claimed to have banned the press from entering his sets until late 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comeback_and_retirement:_1988.E2.80.931992">Comeback and retirement: 19881992</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg/225px-Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg" width="225" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg/338px-Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg 2x" data-file-width="401" data-file-height="425" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabhbachchan28529.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bachchan during the shoot of 1990 Hindi film <i><a href="/wiki/Agneepath_(1990_film)" title="Agneepath (1990 film)">Agneepath</a>.</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1988, Bachchan returned to films, playing the title role in <i><a href="/wiki/Shahenshah_(film)" title="Shahenshah (film)">Shahenshah</a></i>, which was a box office success.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> After the success of his comeback film however, his star power began to wane as all of his subsequent films like <i><a href="/wiki/Jaadugar" title="Jaadugar">Jaadugar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Toofan_(1989_film)" title="Toofan (1989 film)">Toofan</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Main_Azaad_Hoon" title="Main Azaad Hoon">Main Azaad Hoon</a></i> (all released in 1989) failed at the box office. The 1991 hit film, <i><a href="/wiki/Hum_(film)" title="Hum (film)">Hum</a></i>, for which he won his third Filmfare Best Actor Award, looked like it might reverse the trend, but this momentum was short-lived and his string of box office failures continued. Notably, despite the lack of hits, it was during this era that Bachchan won his first <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="National Film Award for Best Actor">National Film Award for Best Actor</a> for his performance as a Mafia don in the 1990 film <i><a href="/wiki/Agneepath_(1990_film)" title="Agneepath (1990 film)">Agneepath</a>.</i> These years would see his last on-screen appearances for some time. After the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Khuda_Gawah" title="Khuda Gawah">Khuda Gawah</a></i> in 1992, Bachchan went into semi-retirement for five years. With the exception of the delayed release of <i><a href="/wiki/Insaniyat_(1994_film)" title="Insaniyat (1994 film)">Insaniyat</a></i> (1994), which was also a box office failure, Bachchan did not appear in any new releases for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-boxoffice1994_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice1994-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Producer_and_acting_comeback_1996.E2.80.9399">Producer and acting comeback 199699</span></h3>
<p>Bachchan turned producer during his temporary retirement period, setting up <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan_Corporation" title="Amitabh Bachchan Corporation">Amitabh Bachchan Corporation</a>, Ltd. (ABCL) in 1996, with a vision of becoming a 10 billion rupees (approx. U.S. $250 M) premier entertainment company by the year 2000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ABCL's strategy was to introduce products and services covering an entire cross-section of India's entertainment industry. ABCL's operations were mainstream commercial film production and distribution, audio cassettes and video discs, production and marketing of television software, and celebrity and event management.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Soon after the company was launched in 1996, the first film it produced was <i><a href="/wiki/Tere_Mere_Sapne_(1996_film)" title="Tere Mere Sapne (1996 film)">Tere Mere Sapne</a>,</i> which did not fare well at the boxoffice but launched the careers of actors like <a href="/wiki/Arshad_Warsi" title="Arshad Warsi">Arshad Warsi</a> and South films star <a href="/wiki/Simran_(actress)" title="Simran (actress)">Simran</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ABCL produced a few other films, none of which did well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1997, Bachchan attempted to make his acting comeback with the film <i><a href="/wiki/Mrityudata" title="Mrityudata">Mrityudata</a></i>, produced by ABCL. Though <i>Mrityudaata</i> attempted to reprise Bachchan's earlier success as an action hero, the film was a failure both financially and critically.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ABCL was the main sponsor of the <i><a href="/wiki/Miss_World_1996" title="Miss World 1996">1996 Miss World beauty pageant</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a> but lost millions. The fiasco and the consequent legal battles surrounding ABCL and various entities after the event, coupled with the fact that ABCL was reported to have overpaid most of its top level managers, eventually led to its financial and operational collapse in 1997. The company went into administration and was later declared a failed company by Indian Industries board.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Bombay high court, in April 1999, restrained Bachchan from selling off his Bombay <a href="/wiki/Bungalow" title="Bungalow">bungalow</a> 'Prateeksha' and two flats till the pending loan recovery cases of <a href="/wiki/Canara_Bank" title="Canara Bank">Canara Bank</a> were disposed of. Bachchan had, however, pleaded that he had mortgaged his bungalow to raise funds for his company.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan attempted to revive his acting career and had average success with <i><a href="/wiki/Bade_Miyan_Chote_Miyan" title="Bade Miyan Chote Miyan">Bade Miyan Chote Miyan</a></i> (1998),<sup id="cite_ref-boxoffice1994_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice1994-50">[50]</a></sup> and received positive reviews for <i><a href="/wiki/Sooryavansham" title="Sooryavansham">Sooryavansham</a></i> (1999)<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> but other films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Lal_Baadshah" title="Lal Baadshah">Lal Baadshah</a></i> (1999) and <i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Ki_Kasam_(1999_film)" title="Hindustan Ki Kasam (1999 film)">Hindustan Ki Kasam</a></i> (1999) were box office failures.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_prominence:_2000.E2.80.93present">Return to prominence: 2000present</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg/220px-Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg/330px-Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg/440px-Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="668" data-file-height="628" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabh_Bachchan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bachchan at the <a href="/wiki/IIFA_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="IIFA Awards">IIFA Awards</a> in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bachan_mohanlal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Bachan_mohanlal.jpg/220px-Bachan_mohanlal.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Bachan_mohanlal.jpg/330px-Bachan_mohanlal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Bachan_mohanlal.jpg/440px-Bachan_mohanlal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="518" data-file-height="364" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bachan_mohanlal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bachchan with <a href="/wiki/Mohanlal" title="Mohanlal">Mohanlal</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2000, Amitabh Bachchan appeared in Yash Chopra's box-office hit, <i><a href="/wiki/Mohabbatein" title="Mohabbatein">Mohabbatein</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Aditya_Chopra" title="Aditya Chopra">Aditya Chopra</a>. He played a stern, older figure that rivalled the character of <a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shahrukh Khan</a>. His role won him his third <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Actor">Filmfare Best Supporting Actor Award</a>. Other hits followed, with Bachchan appearing as an older family patriarch in <i><a href="/wiki/Ek_Rishtaa:_The_Bond_of_Love" title="Ek Rishtaa: The Bond of Love">Ek Rishtaa: The Bond of Love</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Khushi_Kabhie_Gham..." title="Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...">Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...</a></i> (2001) and <i><a href="/wiki/Baghban_(film)" title="Baghban (film)">Baghban</a></i> (2003). As an actor, he continued to perform in a range of characters, receiving critical praise for his performances in <i><a href="/wiki/Aks_(film)" title="Aks (film)">Aks</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Aankhen_(2002_film)" title="Aankhen (2002 film)">Aankhen</a></i> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/Khakee" title="Khakee">Khakee</a></i> (2004) and <i><a href="/wiki/Dev_(film)" title="Dev (film)">Dev</a></i> (2004). His performance in <i>Aks</i> won him his first <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Critics_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actor">Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actor</a>. One project that did particularly well for Bachchan was <a href="/wiki/Sanjay_Leela_Bhansali" title="Sanjay Leela Bhansali">Sanjay Leela Bhansali</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Black_(2005_film)" title="Black (2005 film)">Black</a></i> (2005). The film starred Bachchan as an ageing teacher of a deaf-blind girl and followed their relationship. His performance was unanimously praised by critics and audiences and won him his second National Film Award for Best Actor, his fourth Filmfare Best Actor Award and his second Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actor. Taking advantage of this resurgence, Amitabh began endorsing a variety of products and services, appearing in many television and billboard advertisements. In 2005 and 2006, he starred with his son Abhishek in the hit films <i><a href="/wiki/Bunty_Aur_Babli" title="Bunty Aur Babli">Bunty Aur Babli</a></i> (2005), the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather" title="The Godfather">Godfather</a></i> tribute <i><a href="/wiki/Sarkar_(film)" title="Sarkar (film)">Sarkar</a></i> (2005), and <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Alvida_Naa_Kehna" title="Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna">Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna</a></i> (2006). All of them were successful at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-Starring_with_son_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Starring_with_son-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> His later releases in 2006 and early 2007 were <i><a href="/wiki/Baabul_(2006_film)" title="Baabul (2006 film)">Baabul</a></i> (2006),<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Ekalavya" title="Ekalavya">Ekalavya</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Nishabd" title="Nishabd">Nishabd</a></i> (2007), which failed to do well at the box office but his performances in each of them were praised by critics.<sup id="cite_ref-Bachchan.27s_films_fail_at_the_box_office_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bachchan.27s_films_fail_at_the_box_office-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2007, two of his films <i><a href="/wiki/Cheeni_Kum" title="Cheeni Kum">Cheeni Kum</a></i> and the multi-starrer <i><a href="/wiki/Shootout_at_Lokhandwala" title="Shootout at Lokhandwala">Shootout at Lokhandwala</a></i> were released. <i>Shootout at Lokhandwala</i> did well at the box office and was declared a semi-hit in India, while <i>Cheeni Kum</i> picked up after a slow start and only had average success.<sup id="cite_ref-udxlrh_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-udxlrh-57">[57]</a></sup> A remake of his biggest hit, <i>Sholay</i> (1975), entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Aag_(2007_film)" title="Aag (2007 film)">Ram Gopal Varma Ki Aag</a></i>, released in August of that same year and proved to be a major commercial failure in addition to its poor critical reception.<sup id="cite_ref-udxlrh_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-udxlrh-57">[57]</a></sup> The year also marked Bachchan's first appearance in an English-language film, <a href="/wiki/Rituparno_Ghosh" title="Rituparno Ghosh">Rituparno Ghosh</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Lear" title="The Last Lear">The Last Lear</a></i>, co-starring <a href="/wiki/Arjun_Rampal" title="Arjun Rampal">Arjun Rampal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Preity_Zinta" title="Preity Zinta">Preity Zinta</a>. The film premiered at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2007 Toronto International Film Festival">2007 Toronto International Film Festival</a> on 9 September 2007. He received positive reviews from critics who hailed his performance as his best ever since <i>Black</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Bachchan was slated to play a supporting role in his first international film, <i><a href="/wiki/Shantaram_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shantaram (film)">Shantaram</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Mira_Nair" title="Mira Nair">Mira Nair</a> and starring Hollywood actor <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a> in the lead. The film was due to begin filming in February 2008 but due to the writer's strike, was pushed to September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Hollywood_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollywood-59">[59]</a></sup> The film is currently "shelved" indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vivek_Sharma" title="Vivek Sharma">Vivek Sharma</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Bhoothnath" title="Bhoothnath">Bhoothnath</a></i>, in which he plays the title role as a ghost, was released on 9 May 2008. <i><a href="/wiki/Sarkar_Raj" title="Sarkar Raj">Sarkar Raj</a></i>, the sequel of the 2005 film <i>Sarkar</i>, released in June 2008 and received a positive response at the box-office. <i><a href="/wiki/Paa_(film)" title="Paa (film)">Paa</a></i>, which released at the end of 2009 was a highly anticipated project as it saw him playing his own son Abhishek's Progeria-affected 13-year-old son, and it opened to favourable reviews, particularly towards Bachchan's performance. It won him his third National Film Award for Best Actor and fifth Filmfare Best Actor Award. In 2010, he debuted in <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_cinema" title="Malayalam cinema">Malayalam film</a> through <i><a href="/wiki/Kandahar_(2010_film)" title="Kandahar (2010 film)">Kandahar</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Major_Ravi" title="Major Ravi">Major Ravi</a> and co-starring <a href="/wiki/Mohanlal" title="Mohanlal">Mohanlal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The film was based on the hijacking incident of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines_Flight_814" title="Indian Airlines Flight 814">Indian Airlines Flight 814</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Bachchan declined any remuneration for this film.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In 2013 he made his Hollywood debut in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gatsby_(2013_film)" title="The Great Gatsby (2013 film)">The Great Gatsby</a></i> making a special appearance opposite <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">Tobey Maguire</a>. In 2014, he played the role of the friendly ghost in the sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Bhoothnath_Returns" title="Bhoothnath Returns">Bhoothnath Returns</a></i>. The next year, he played the role of a grumpy father suffering from chronic constipation in <i><a href="/wiki/Piku" title="Piku">Piku</a></i>. It won him his fourth National Film Award for Best Actor and his third Filmfare Critics Award for Best Actor. Bachchan will next appear in <a href="/wiki/Ram_Gopal_Varma" title="Ram Gopal Varma">Ram Gopal Varma</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Sarkar_3" title="Sarkar 3">Sarkar 3</a></i>. He has also committed to starring in <i><a href="/wiki/Thugs_Of_Hindostan" class="mw-redirect" title="Thugs Of Hindostan">Thugs Of Hindostan</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_career">Television career</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg/170px-Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg" width="170" height="325" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg/255px-Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg/340px-Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="1117" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabh_Bachchan_KBC5_Press.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Amitabh Bachchan at KBC-5 Press Meet</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2000, Bachchan hosted the first season of <i><a href="/wiki/Kaun_Banega_Crorepati" title="Kaun Banega Crorepati">Kaun Banega Crorepati</a></i> (<i>KBC</i>), the Indian adaptation of the British television game show, <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Be_a_Millionaire%3F" title="Who Wants to Be a Millionaire?">Who Wants to Be a Millionaire?</a></i>. The show was well received.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> A second season followed in 2005 but its run was cut short by <a href="/wiki/Star_Plus" title="Star Plus">STAR Plus</a> when Bachchan fell ill in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, Bachchan hosted the <a href="/wiki/Bigg_Boss_3" title="Bigg Boss 3">third season</a> of the reality show <i><a href="/wiki/Bigg_Boss" title="Bigg Boss">Bigg Boss</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Bachchan hosted the fourth season of <i>KBC</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The fifth season started on 15 August 2011 and ended on 17 November 2011. The show became a massive hit with audiences and broke many TRP Records. CNN IBN awarded Indian of the Year- Entertainment to Team KBC and Bachchan. The Show also grabbed all the major Awards for its category.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Bachchan continued to host KBC until 2014.</p>
<p>The sixth season was also hosted by Bachchan, commencing on 7 September 2012, broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Television" title="Sony Pictures Television">Sony TV</a> and received the highest number of viewers thus far.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, he debuted in the fictional <a href="/wiki/Sony_Entertainment_Television" title="Sony Entertainment Television">Sony Entertainment Television</a> TV series titled <i><a href="/wiki/Yudh_(TV_series)" title="Yudh (TV series)">Yudh</a></i> playing the lead role of a businessman battling both his personal and professional life.<sup id="cite_ref-ix_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ix-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan is also the brand ambassador for Gujarat Tourism, which he has been since 1 February 2010.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice">Voice</span></h3>
<p>Bachchan is known for his deep, baritone voice. He has been a narrator, a <a href="/wiki/Playback_singer" title="Playback singer">playback singer</a>, and presenter for numerous programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Renowned film director <a href="/wiki/Satyajit_Ray" title="Satyajit Ray">Satyajit Ray</a> was so impressed with Bachchan's voice that he decided to use Bachchan as the narrator in his 1977 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chess_Players_(film)" title="The Chess Players (film)">Shatranj Ke Khilari</a></i> (The Chess Players).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Bachchan lent his voice as a narrator to the 2001 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Lagaan" title="Lagaan">Lagaan</a></i> which was a super hit.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In 2005, Bachchan lent his voice to the Oscar-winning French documentary <i><a href="/wiki/March_of_the_Penguins" title="March of the Penguins">March of the Penguins</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Luc_Jacquet" title="Luc Jacquet">Luc Jacquet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>He also done voice over work for the following movies:</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Balika_Badhu_(1976_film)" title="Balika Badhu (1976 film)">Balika Badhu</a></i> (1975)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tere_Mere_Sapne_(1996_film)" title="Tere Mere Sapne (1996 film)">Tere Mere Sapne</a> <i>(1996)</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lagaan" title="Lagaan">Lagaan</a> (2001)</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Parineeta_(2005_film)" title="Parineeta (2005 film)">Parineeta</a></i> (2005)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Jodhaa_Akbar" title="Jodhaa Akbar">Jodhaa Akbar</a></i> (2008)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Swami_(2007_film)" title="Swami (2007 film)">Swami</a></i> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Zor_Lagaa_Ke...Haiya!" title="Zor Lagaa Ke...Haiya!">Zor Lagaa Ke...Haiya!</a></i> (2009)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Kahaani" title="Kahaani">Kahaani</a></i> (2012)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Krrish_3" title="Krrish 3">Krrish 3</a></i> (2013)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Mahabharat_(2013_film)" title="Mahabharat (2013 film)">Mahabharat</a></i> (2013)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Kochadaiiyaan" title="Kochadaiiyaan">Kochadaiiyaan (Hindi Version)</a></i> (2014)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_causes">Humanitarian causes</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BachchanAmitabh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/BachchanAmitabh.jpg/220px-BachchanAmitabh.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/BachchanAmitabh.jpg/330px-BachchanAmitabh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/BachchanAmitabh.jpg/440px-BachchanAmitabh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="372" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BachchanAmitabh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bachchan speaking at a function in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Amitabh Bachchan has been involved in many social works. Amitabh donated <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>11 lakh</span> (US$16,000) to clear the debts of nearly 40 beleaguered farmers in Andhra Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> He also donated <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>30 lakh</span> (US$45,000) to clear the debts of some 100 Vidarbha farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In 2010, he donated <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>11 lakh</span> (US$16,000) for <a href="/wiki/Resul_Pookutty" title="Resul Pookutty">Resul Pookutty</a>'s foundation, for medical centre at Kochi.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Amitabh Bachchan donated <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>2.5 lakh</span> (US$3,700) to Delhi Police constable Subhash Chand Tomar's family, who died after succumbing to injuries during anti-gangrape protest for <a href="/wiki/2012_Delhi_gang_rape" title="2012 Delhi gang rape">2012 Delhi gang rape</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> He opened a Harivansh Rai Bachchan Memorial Trust, or HRB Memorial Trust in his father's name in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Amitabh Bachchan was made <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> goodwill ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a> Eradication Campaign in India in 2002, when 1,556 polio cases were detected that year .<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> On 27 March 2014, <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) declared India a polio free country with no case of disease being reported in the previous three years.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In 2013, Amitabh and his family donated <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>25 lakh</span> (US$37,000) to charitable trust Plan India, that works for the upliftment of the girl child in India.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Amitabh Bachchan donated <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>11 lakh</span> (US$16,000) to Maharashtra Police Welfare Fund in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Amitabh was the face of 'Save Our Tigers' campaign that promoted the importance of tiger conservation in India.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_of_India_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_of_India-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amitabh also supported <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a> India's campaign to free, Sunder, a 14-year-old elephant who was chained and tortured in a temple in Kolhapur, Maharashtra.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> After the elephant was freed and rehabilitated in <a href="/wiki/Bannerghatta_National_Park" title="Bannerghatta National Park">Bannerghatta National Park</a> in Bangalore, he was reported to tweet, "@PetaIndia has turned elephant Sunders home into free-roaming, forested sanctuary... feeling good I contributed to this cause&#160;!"<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, it was announced that he had recorded his voice and lent his image to the Hindi and English language versions of the <a href="/wiki/TeachAIDS" title="TeachAIDS">TeachAIDS</a> software, an international <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> prevention education tool developed at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_investments">Business investments</span></h2>
<p>Amitabh Bachchan has invested in many upcoming business ventures. In 2013, he bought a 10% stake in Just Dial from which he made a gain of 4600 percent. He holds a 3.4% equity in Stampede Capital, a financial technology firm specializing in cloud computing for financial markets. The Bachchan family also bought shares worth $252,000 in Meridian Tech, a consulting company in U.S. Recently they made their first overseas investment in Ziddu.com, a cloud based content distribution platform.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_of_India_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_of_India-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards.2C_honours_and_recognitions">Awards, honours and recognitions</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Amitabh_Bachchan" title="List of awards and nominations received by Amitabh Bachchan">List of awards and nominations received by Amitabh Bachchan</a></div>
<p>Apart from National Film Awards, <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> and other competitive awards which Bachchan won for his performances throughout the years, he has been awarded several honours for his achievements in the Indian film industry. In 1991, he became the first artist to receive the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Filmfare Lifetime Achievement Award">Filmfare Lifetime Achievement Award</a>, which was established in the name of <a href="/wiki/Raj_Kapoor" title="Raj Kapoor">Raj Kapoor</a>. Bachchan was crowned as <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Special_Award" title="Filmfare Special Award">Superstar of the Millennium</a> in 2000 at the Filmfare Awards.</p>
<p>In 1999, Bachchan was voted the "greatest star of stage or screen" in a BBC <i>Your Millennium</i> online poll. The organisation noted that "Many people in the western world will not have heard of [him]&#160;... [but it] is a reflection of the huge popularity of Indian films."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In 2001, he was honoured with the Actor of the Century award at the <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_International_Film_Festival" title="Alexandria International Film Festival">Alexandria International Film Festival</a> in Egypt in recognition of his contribution to the world of cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Many other honours for his achievements were conferred upon him at several International Film Festivals, including the Lifetime Achievement Award at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Asian_Film_Awards" title="Asian Film Awards">Asian Film Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2000, he became the first living Asian to have been modeled in wax at London's <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> Wax Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Another statue was installed in New York in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Hong Kong in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Washington, DC in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and Delhi, in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, he was conferred with the Honorary Citizenship of the French town of <a href="/wiki/Deauville" title="Deauville">Deauville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Civilian Awards</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Government of India awarded him with the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Shri" title="Padma Shri">Padma Shri</a> in 1984, the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Bhushan" title="Padma Bhushan">Padma Bhushan</a> in 2001 and the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Vibhushan" title="Padma Vibhushan">Padma Vibhushan</a> in 2015. France's highest civilian honour, the Knight of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a>, was conferred upon him by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_France" title="Government of France">French Government</a> in 2007 for his "exceptional career in the world of cinema and beyond".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>Honoured with an Honorary Doctorate</b></p>
<ul>
<li>In 2004, by the University of <a href="/wiki/Jhansi" title="Jhansi">Jhansi</a>, India,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2006, by the University of Delhi<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2006, by the <a href="/wiki/De_Montfort_University" title="De Montfort University">De Montfort University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, UK<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2007, by the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Beckett_University" title="Leeds Beckett University">Leeds Metropolitan University</a> in Yorkshire, UK<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2011, by the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_University_of_Technology" title="Queensland University of Technology">Queensland University of Technology</a> in Brisbane, Australia<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2013, by the <a href="/wiki/Jodhpur_National_University" title="Jodhpur National University">Jodhpur National University</a><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2015, by the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Arts_(Egypt)" title="Academy of Arts (Egypt)">Academy of Arts (Egypt)</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg/220px-Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg/330px-Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg/440px-Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3273" data-file-height="2646" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amitabh_Bachchan_with_Olympic_torch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Amitabh Bachchan with the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_flame" title="Olympic flame">Olympic flame</a> in London on 27 July 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 27 July 2012, Bachchan carried the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_flame" title="Olympic flame">Olympic torch</a> during the last leg of its relay in London's Southwark.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Severals books have been written about Bachchan. <i>Amitabh Bachchan: the Legend</i> was published in 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <i>To be or not to be: Amitabh Bachchan</i> in 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <i>AB: The Legend (A Photographer's Tribute)</i> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> <i>Amitabh Bachchan: Ek Jeevit Kimvadanti</i> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> <i>Amitabh: The Making of a Superstar</i> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> <i>Looking for the Big B: Bollywood, Bachchan and Me</i> in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> and <i>Bachchanalia</i> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bachchan himself wrote a book in 2002: <i>Soul Curry for you and me&#160; An Empowering Philosophy That Can Enrich Your Life</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In the early 80s, Bachchan authorised the use of his likeness for the comic book character <a href="/wiki/Supremo_(comics)" title="Supremo (comics)">Supremo</a> in a series titled <i>The Adventures of Amitabh Bachchan</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> In May 2014, <a href="/wiki/La_Trobe_University" title="La Trobe University">La Trobe University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> named a Scholarship after Bachchan.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was named "Hottest Vegetarian" by PETA India in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> He won the title of "Asia's Sexiest Vegetarian" in a contest poll run by PETA Asia<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorials">Memorials</span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Bachchan_Sports_Complex" title="Amitabh Bachchan Sports Complex">Amitabh Bachchan Sports Complex</a> in Allahbad managed by UP Sports Directorate is named after him.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Also a road is named after him as Amitabh Bachhan Road in his home town, <a href="/wiki/Allahabad" title="Allahabad">Allahabad</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>There is a temple in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, where Amitabh is worshipped as a God.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The tiles of the temple are adorned with words Jai Shri Amitabh; in place of the idol, you see his photo and a pair of white shoes that the actor wore in his movie, <a href="/wiki/Agneepath_(1990_film)" title="Agneepath (1990 film)">Agneepath</a><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>

"Lyrical Nationalism: Gender, Friendship, and Excess in 1970s Hindi Cinema". <i>The Velvet Light Trap</i>. <b>51</b> (1): 4353. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1353%2Fvlt.2003.0007">10.1353/vlt.2003.0007</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/1542-4251">1542-4251</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAmitabh+Bachchan&amp;rft.atitle=Lyrical+Nationalism%3A+Gender%2C+Friendship%2C+and+Excess+in+1970s+Hindi+Cinema&amp;rft.aufirst=Priya&amp;rft.aulast=Jha&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1353%2Fvlt.2003.0007&amp;rft.issn=1542-4251&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Velvet+Light+Trap&amp;rft.pages=43-53&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=51" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
